2:19:1063:0:14:71:282:708:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Persistence of Power, Elites and Institutions
2:20:1108:14:14:71:270:694:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Daron Acemoglu and James A. Robinson
2:21:1144:14:14:71:232:680:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:NBER Working Paper No. 12108
2:22:1172:14:14:71:129:666:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:March 2006
2:23:1182:14:29:71:206:652:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:JEL No. H2, N10, N40, P16
2:24:1207:29:28:273:338:623:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:F:ABSTRACT
2:25:1215:28:20:71:539:595:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:We construct a model of simultaneous change and persistence in institutions. The model consists of
2:26:1313:20:20:71:539:575:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:landowning  elites  and  workers,  and  the  key  economic  decision  concerns  the  form  of  economic
2:27:1416:20:19:71:539:555:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:institutions regulating the transaction of labor (e.g., competitive markets versus labor repression).
2:28:1517:19:20:71:539:536:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:The main idea is that equilibrium economic institutions are a result of the exercise of de jure and de
2:29:1619:20:20:71:539:516:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:facto political power. A change in political institutions, for example a move from nondemocracy to
2:30:1717:20:20:71:539:496:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:democracy,  alters  the  distribution  of  de  jure  political  power,  but  the  elite  can  intensify  their
2:31:1827:20:20:71:539:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:investments in de facto political power, such as lobbying or the use of paramilitary forces, to partially
2:32:1932:20:19:71:539:456:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:or fully offset their loss of de jure power. In the baseline model, equilibrium changes in political
2:33:2032:19:20:71:539:437:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:institutions  have  no  effect  on  the  (stochastic)  equilibrium  distribution  of  economic  institutions,
2:34:2141:20:20:71:539:417:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:leading  to  a  particular  form  of  persistence  in  equilibrium  institutions,  which  we  refer  to  as
2:35:2248:20:20:71:539:397:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:invariance. When the model is enriched to allow for limits on the exercise of de facto power by the
2:36:2347:20:20:71:539:377:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:elite in democracy or for costs of changing economic institutions, the equilibrium takes the form of
2:37:2447:20:19:71:539:357:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:a Markov regime-switching process with state dependence. Finally, when we allow for the possibility
2:38:2546:19:20:71:539:338:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:that changing political institutions is more difficult than altering economic institutions, the model
2:39:2647:20:20:71:539:318:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:leads to a pattern of captured democracy, whereby a democratic regime may survive, but choose
2:40:2740:20:20:71:539:298:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:economic institutions favoring the elite. The main ideas featuring in the model are illustrated using
2:41:2841:20:34:71:399:278:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:historical examples from the U.S. South, Latin America and Liberia.
2:42:2908:34:14:71:154:244:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Daron Acemoglu
2:43:2922:14:14:71:197:230:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Department of Economics
2:44:2945:14:14:71:148:216:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:MIT, E52-380B
2:45:2958:14:14:71:164:202:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:50 Memorial Drive
2:46:2975:14:15:71:210:188:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Cambridge, MA 02142-1347
2:47:2999:15:14:71:123:173:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:and NBER
2:48:3007:14:0:71:146:159:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:daron@mit.edu
2:49:3020:0:14:323:416:244:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:James A. Robinson
2:50:3037:14:14:323:416:230:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Harvard University
2:51:3055:14:14:323:455:216:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Department of Government
2:52:3079:14:14:323:467:202:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:N309, 1737 Cambridge Street
2:53:3106:14:15:323:434:188:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:Cambridge, MA 02138
2:54:3125:15:14:323:375:173:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:and NBER
2:55:3133:14:0:323:457:159:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:F:jrobinson@gov.harvard.edu
3:56:3158:0:22:110:370:700:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:“Plus ça change plus c’est la même chose.” French Proverb.
3:57:3216:22:19:110:502:678:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:“The domination of an organized minority ... over the unorganized majority is inevitable.
3:58:3305:19:18:110:502:659:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:The power of any minority is irresistible as against each single individual in the majority,
3:59:3397:18:19:110:502:641:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:who stands alone before the totality of theorganized minority.  At the same time, the
3:60:3482:19:18:110:502:622:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:minority is organized for the very reason that it is a minority.” Gaetano Mosca (1939, p.
3:61:3571:18:34:110:127:604:100:g_d0_f3:100:g_d0_f3:F:53).
3:62:3575:34:30:82:211:570:209:g_d0_f4:209:g_d0_f4:C:1Introduction
3:63:3588:30:18:82:529:540:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Current empirical work and theoretical discussions of the impact of institutions on economic
3:64:3680:18:19:82:529:522:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:development either implicitly or explicitly assume that institutions persist (e.g., North, 1990,
3:65:3776:19:18:82:528:503:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Engerman and Sokoloff, 1997, Acemoglu, Johnson and Robinson, 2001, 2002). In fact, some of
3:66:3866:18:18:82:529:485:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the most popular empirical strategies in gauging the effect of institutions on economic perfor-
3:67:3961:18:19:82:528:467:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:mance use the persistence of institutions over centuries as part of their conceptual approach
3:68:4054:19:18:82:529:448:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and identification strategy. But many aspects of “institutions” show substantial change over
3:69:4146:18:19:82:528:430:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:periods much shorter than a century. Many less-developed countries, especially those in Latin
3:70:4239:19:18:82:528:411:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:America and Africa, have changed their political institutions all too often over the past 100
3:71:4332:18:19:82:528:393:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:years, with frequent switches between democracy and dictatorship (see, e.g., Acemoglu and
3:72:4421:19:18:82:354:374:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:Robinson, 2006a) and multiple changes in constitutions.1
3:73:4477:18:18:99:528:356:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The same pattern also emerges when we turn to economic institutions. For example, while
3:74:4564:18:19:82:528:338:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:many historians and economists trace the economic problems of Latin America to colonial labor
3:75:4657:19:18:82:528:319:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:practices such as theencomiendaor themita, and those of the Caribbean to slavery and to the
3:76:4748:18:19:82:529:301:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:plantation complex, all of these economic institutions vanished long ago.2Beneath this pattern
3:77:4842:19:18:82:528:282:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of change, however, economic systems often show surprising continuity. The form of agricul-
3:78:4933:18:19:82:528:264:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tural labor relations in many of the Latin American and Caribbean countries changed little
3:79:5023:19:18:82:529:245:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:after colonialism, and perhaps relatedly, these societies continued to suffer various economic
3:80:5117:18:18:82:529:227:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:problems, slow growth, and economic and political instability throughout the 20th century.
3:81:5207:18:19:82:528:209:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Another interesting example comes from the U.S. South. Even though slavery was abolished
3:82:5295:19:18:82:528:190:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:at the end of the Civil War, the U.S. South maintained a remarkably similar agricultural sys-
3:83:5388:18:16:82:528:172:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tem, based on large plantations and low-wage uneducated labor, and remained relatively poor
3:84:5479:16:15:95:529:156:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:1For instance, Colombia had 8 constitutions in the 19th century (Gibson, 1948), while Bolivia had 11 (Trigo,
3:85:5587:15:7:82:284:141:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:1958) and Peru 9 (Palacios and Guillergua, 2003).
3:86:5636:7:15:95:529:134:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:2In Latin America, the last form of official forced labor,pongueaje, was abolished in Bolivia in 1952 (Klein,
3:87:5745:15:11:82:529:119:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:1992, Chapter 8). Unpaid labor services lasted in Guatemala until 1945 (McCreery, 1994). Slaves were gradually
3:88:5855:11:11:82:529:108:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:freed, for example in 1850 in Colombia. In the British Caribbean slavery was abolished after 1834, though it
3:89:5963:11:0:82:275:97:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:lasted until in 1886 in Cuba and 1888 in Brazil.
4:90:6012:0:18:82:256:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:until the middle of the 20th century.
4:91:6049:18:18:99:529:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In this paper, we provide a possible explanation for this paradoxical pattern of the coexis-
4:92:6141:18:19:82:528:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tence of frequent changes in political institutions with the persistence in certain (important)
4:93:6236:19:18:82:529:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:aspects of economic institutions.3Our approach illustrates the possibility of two different types
4:94:6333:18:19:82:532:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of persistence. The baseline model leads to a pattern which we refer to asinvariance,whereby
4:95:6425:19:18:82:529:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:a change in political institutions from nondemocracy to democracy leads to no change in the
4:96:6516:18:19:82:528:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(stochastic) equilibrium process of economic institutions and of the distribution of resources
4:97:6610:19:18:82:528:571:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in society. Simple extensions of our baseline model lead to a richer form of persistence, which
4:98:6705:18:18:82:528:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:we refer to asstate dependence; the probability that a society will be democratic (and have
4:99:6796:18:19:82:523:535:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:pro-citizen economic institutions) tomorrow is a function of whether it is democratic today.4
4:100:6889:19:18:99:528:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The underlying idea of our approach is that equilibrium economic institutions emerge from
4:101:6978:18:19:82:533:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the interaction between political institutions, which allocatede jure political power,andthe
4:102:7070:19:18:82:529:479:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:distribution ofde facto political poweracross social groups (see Acemoglu and Robinson, 2006a,
4:103:7164:18:18:82:528:461:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and Acemoglu, Johnson and Robinson, 2005b). De Facto power is power that is not allocated
4:104:7253:18:19:82:529:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:by institutions (such as elections), but rather ispossessed by groups as a result of their wealth,
4:105:7351:19:18:82:528:424:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:weapons or ability to solve the collective action problem. A change in political institutions
4:106:7444:18:19:82:528:406:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that modifies the distribution of de jure power need not lead to a change in the equilibrium
4:107:7536:19:18:82:529:387:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:process for economic institutions if it is associated with an offsetting change in the distribution
4:108:7635:18:19:82:529:369:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of de facto political power (e.g., in the form of bribery, capture of the political parties, or use of
4:109:7737:19:18:82:528:350:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:paramilitaries). The central argument in this paper is that there is a natural reason to expect
4:110:7832:18:18:82:529:332:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:changes in the distribution of de facto political power to partially or entirely offset changes
4:111:7927:18:19:82:528:314:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in de jure power brought about by reforms in specific political institutions as long as these
4:112:8020:19:18:82:528:295:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:reforms do not radically alter the political structure of society, the identity of the elites, or the
4:113:8121:18:19:82:265:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:source of economic rents for the elites.
4:114:8161:19:18:99:529:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:To make these ideas precise, we develop a model consisting of two groups, a landed elite
4:115:8249:18:16:82:528:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and the citizens. The key economic institution concerns the organization of the labor mar-
4:116:8339:16:15:95:529:224:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:3Throughout, persistence refers to the continuity of acluster of institutions, for example, the extent of
4:117:8444:15:11:82:528:209:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:enforcement of property rights for a broad cross-section of society. Lack of property rights enforcement may have
4:118:8557:11:11:82:529:198:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:its roots in quite different specific economic institutions, for example, risk of expropriation by the government
4:119:8670:11:11:82:529:187:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:or elites; extreme corruption; economic systems such as serfdom or slavery preventing large segments of the
4:120:8777:11:11:82:528:176:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:population from selling their labor freely or from investing in most economic activities; legal rules making it
4:121:8888:11:11:82:528:165:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:impossible for those without political connections to have their contracts enforced; or entry barriers creating a
4:122:9001:11:7:82:173:154:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:non-level playingfield.
4:123:9024:7:15:95:528:147:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:4We refer to this type of persistence as “state dependence”since the probability distribution over equilibrium
4:124:9134:15:11:82:528:132:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:political and economic institutions tomorrow depends on the “state” of the system, which is political institutions
4:125:9248:11:10:82:529:121:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:today. See Page (2006) for a discussion of richer forms of persistence in political systems, where the past entire
4:126:9362:10:0:82:500:111:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:sequence of events, rather than simply a low-dimensional state vector, might influence future outcomes.
5:127:9466:0:18:82:529:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ket, in particular, whether wages are competitive or are repressed below this level.5In the
5:128:9557:18:18:82:529:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:model, economic institutions are decided either by the landed elite or the citizens (workers)
5:129:9650:18:19:82:529:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:depending on who has more political power. Political power, in turn, is determined by both
5:130:9740:19:18:82:529:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political institutions that allocate de jure power and the distribution of de facto power, which
5:131:9836:18:19:82:529:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is derived, at least partly, from a social group’s ability to solve their collective action problem.
5:132:9936:19:18:82:528:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:A key observation is that landowners, by virtue of their smaller numbers and their established
5:133:10030:18:19:82:529:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:position, have a comparative advantage in solving the collective action problem (Mosca, 1939,
5:134:10123:19:18:82:528:571:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Olson, 1965). This implies that the amount of de facto political power of the elite is an equi-
5:135:10218:18:18:82:528:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:librium outcome, and responds to incentives. Nevertheless, political institutions and de jure
5:136:10311:18:19:82:528:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political power also matter for equilibrium outcomes. For example, in democracy de jure po-
5:137:10402:19:18:82:528:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:litical power is allocated to the majority, so the balance of power is tilted towards the citizens
5:138:10500:18:19:82:529:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(see Acemoglu and Robinson, 2006a). In addition, freedom of political organization and the
5:139:10590:19:18:82:529:479:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:existence of political parties may help the citizens in solving their collective action problem
5:140:10685:18:18:82:435:461:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:more effectively, thus facilitating their exercise of de facto political power.
5:141:10764:18:19:99:529:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In the model society, in every period there is a “contest” between the elite and the citizens,
5:142:10858:19:18:82:529:424:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and political institutions (democracy versusnondemocracy) determine how level the playing
5:143:10947:18:19:82:529:406:121:g_d0_f6:121:g_d0_f3:B:field is in this contest.  Those with greater political power determine economic institutions
5:144:11040:19:18:82:529:387:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:today and political institutions tomorrow. The most interesting result of our framework is
5:145:11130:18:19:82:528:369:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that, because the elite’s de facto political power is an equilibrium outcome, it will partly or
5:146:11225:19:18:82:528:350:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:entirely offset the effect of changes in political institutions. In particular, the elite will invest
5:147:11326:18:18:82:440:332:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:more in their de facto political power in democracy than in nondemocracy.
5:148:11399:18:19:99:528:314:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In the baseline model, this effect is sufficiently strong that the distribution of equilibrium
5:149:11493:19:18:82:528:295:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:economic institutions is identical in democracy and nondemocracy–thus leading to the pattern
5:150:11585:18:19:82:529:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of invariance defined above.6This pattern shows that it could be mistaken to infer from
5:151:11672:19:18:82:529:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:frequent changes in certain dimensions of political institutions that there is little institutional
5:152:11771:18:19:82:534:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:persistence.  The result also starkly illustrates how changes in some specificdimensionsof
5:153:11861:19:18:82:529:221:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political institutions can be undone by the greater exercise of de facto political power by the
5:154:11956:18:18:82:105:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:elite.
5:155:11962:18:19:99:528:185:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Even though in this baseline model the equilibrium probability distribution of economic
5:156:12049:19:18:82:528:166:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:institutions is independent of whether the society is democratic or nondemocratic, this prob-
5:157:12142:18:16:82:529:148:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ability distribution is still affected by economic fundamentals. The comparative static results
5:158:12237:16:15:95:529:132:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:5Although this setup is natural from the view point of Latin American history, it is not essential to the
5:159:12342:15:7:82:111:117:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:results.
5:160:12350:7:15:95:529:110:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:6To be precise, therearechanges in economic institutions, but theequilibrium distributionof economic
5:161:12450:15:0:82:276:95:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:institutions isinvariantto political institutions.
6:162:12501:0:18:82:528:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:illustrate this. The most interesting among these is that the economic structure of the society,
6:163:12597:18:18:82:528:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:for example the presence of sectors competing with agriculture for labor, will have a major
6:164:12688:18:19:82:529:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:effect on the equilibrium. The more productive are these sectors, the less the elite have to gain
6:165:12785:19:18:82:528:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:from using repressive methods, and the more likely it is that institutions favor the citizens.
6:166:12879:18:19:82:528:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Second, the smaller the numbers of the elite, the more cohesive they are and the more able they
6:167:12974:19:18:82:528:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:will be to solve the collective action problem and choose the institutions they favor. Finally,
6:168:13069:18:19:82:528:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and more paradoxically, the political advantage created by a democracy for the citizens may
6:169:13160:19:18:82:528:571:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:lead to a greater domination of politics by the elite. This result followsbecause the democratic
6:170:13256:18:18:82:528:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:advantage of the citizens creates a future cost for the elite and they are willing to invest more in
6:171:13356:18:19:82:529:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:activities to increase their de facto power to avoid this future cost.7However, when democratic
6:172:13451:19:18:82:529:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:institutions create a sufficiently large political advantage for the citizens (i.e., when they are
6:173:13549:18:19:82:529:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:“sufficiently strong”), the nature of the equilibrium changes qualitatively, and democracy may
6:174:13643:19:18:82:212:479:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:become an absorbing state.
6:175:13669:18:18:99:528:461:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The invariance result, that the de facto political power of the elite canentirelyoffset
6:176:13756:18:19:82:529:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the effect of changes in political institutions, is special. In the rest of the paper, we extend
6:177:13852:19:18:82:529:424:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:our baseline model in a number of ways to show how, more generally, the de facto political
6:178:13942:18:19:82:528:406:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:power of the eliteonly partiallyundoes the effect of changes in political institutions, leading
6:179:14037:19:18:82:529:387:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to an equilibrium with a Markov regime-switching structure. The two extensions we consider
6:180:14127:18:19:82:528:369:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:allow democracy to place limits on the exercise of de facto power by the elite (e.g., limits on
6:181:14222:19:18:82:529:350:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:their use of paramilitaries or co-option of politicians) and introduce the feature that changing
6:182:14318:18:18:82:529:332:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:economic institutions may be difficult in the short run (e.g., because the democratic regime
6:183:14410:18:19:82:529:314:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:has already implemented some changes favoring the citizens). Both of these extensions lead
6:184:14500:19:18:82:528:295:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to an equilibrium structure where the society switches between democracy and nondemocracy,
6:185:14590:18:19:82:529:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:with different sets of economic institutions in the two regimes, and exhibits state dependence
6:186:14684:19:18:82:528:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(so that nondemocracy is more likely to follow nondemocracy than it is to follow democracy).
6:187:14776:18:19:99:535:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, we analyze a richer model in which political institutions are moredurable,in
6:188:14861:19:18:82:529:221:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:thesensethat,indemocracy,itismoredifficult for the elite to change political institutions
6:189:14950:18:18:82:529:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f7:B:than economic institutions. This model leads to a phenomenon which we refer to ascaptured
6:190:15039:18:19:82:528:185:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:B:democracy; the equilibrium may feature the emergence and persistence of democracy for a
6:191:15126:19:15:82:528:166:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:long span of time, but throughout the economic institutions will be those favoring the elite. In
6:192:15222:15:15:95:529:151:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:7It is also interesting that in this baseline model, there is greater inefficiency in democracy than in non-
6:193:15330:15:11:82:528:136:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:democracy, because in democracy the economic allocations are the same as in nondemocracy, but there is
6:194:15432:11:11:82:529:125:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:greater exercise of de facto political power by the elite,which is costly. This result suggests some insights about
6:195:15547:11:11:82:529:114:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:why certain potential reforms in specific political institutions in many less-developed countries may have failed
6:196:15660:11:11:82:529:103:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:to generate significant economic growth and also perhaps about why the post-war economic performance of
6:197:15763:11:0:82:424:92:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:democracies may have been no better than those of dictatorships (e.g., Barro, 1997).
7:198:15848:0:18:82:528:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:fact, somewhat paradoxically, this extended model predicts that the equilibrium probability
7:199:15939:18:18:82:529:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of labor-repressive institutions is higher in democracy than in nondemocracy, motivating the
7:200:16031:18:19:82:207:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:term captured democracy.
7:201:16055:19:18:99:528:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The model also sheds some light on how institutional persistence can be diminished or
7:202:16140:18:19:82:528:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:broken.  It suggests that an effective democracy requires both reforms in specific political
7:203:16232:19:18:82:528:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:institutions (such as voting rules or electoral procedures), but also a way of curbing the de
7:204:16325:18:19:82:528:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:facto political power of the elite, which can be achieved directly, for example, by reducing their
7:205:16423:19:18:82:528:571:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ability to capture the political system, or indirectly by reforming the economic structure so
7:206:16516:18:18:82:442:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that with reduced land rents, they have less incentive to thwart democracy.
7:207:16591:18:19:99:529:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The model’s insights enable us to interpret the experience of many less developed countries
7:208:16682:19:18:82:529:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in a different light. For example, in the Americas, labor repression was of central importance
7:209:16776:18:19:82:534:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:during the colonial era, and was achieved by various means including theencomienda,the
7:210:16862:19:18:82:529:479:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:B:mita, and slavery.  Yet repression did not end when themitaand slavery were abolished.
7:211:16948:18:18:82:528:461:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:It continued with domination of politics by local landed elites, with the creation of labor
7:212:17039:18:19:82:529:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:market monopsonies (Solberg, 1969, McGreevey, 1971, Coatsworth, 1974, McCreery, 1986),
7:213:17125:19:18:82:528:424:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and the systematic threat of violence against peasants in rural areas. Similarly, in the sugar
7:214:17219:18:19:82:528:406:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:plantations of the British Caribbean, Natal or Mauritius, slavery was replaced by the use of
7:215:17311:19:18:82:528:387:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:cheap indentured laborers from the Indian subcontinent (Tinker, 1974, Northrup, 1995). In the
7:216:17404:18:19:82:529:369:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:U.S. South, slavery was replaced by monopsonistic arrangements, policies designed to impede
7:217:17495:19:18:82:469:350:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:labor mobility, political disenfranchisement, intimidation, violence and lynching.8
7:218:17578:18:18:99:529:332:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Our paper is related to the literature on the persistence of institutions in political science
7:219:17672:18:19:82:528:314:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:(e.g., Steinmo, Thelen and Longstreth, 1992, Pierson, 2004, Thelen, 2004), though much of
7:220:17761:19:18:82:528:295:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:this literature focuses on how specific institutions persist over long periods of time. In this
7:221:17856:18:19:82:529:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:it follows works on ‘hysteresis’ by David (1985) and Arthur (1989) on the lock-in of specific
7:222:17949:19:18:82:528:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:technologies based on increasing returns. In addition to these approaches, persistence of insti-
7:223:18045:18:19:82:528:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tutions can arise in models in which social conventions or norms emerge from local interactions
7:224:18140:19:18:82:528:221:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and learning (e.g., Young, 1998, Bednar and Page, 2006), and in models in which agents make
7:225:18231:18:16:82:528:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:specific investments in activities whose value would be destroyed by changes in social arrange-
7:226:18326:16:15:95:529:187:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:8This discussion and the general approach in the paper beg the question of how the elite are able to exercise
7:227:18435:15:11:82:528:172:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:de facto political power in democracy. This is also discussed in detail in Section 7, where we present a number
7:228:18546:11:11:82:529:161:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:of historical case studies illustrating the pattern ofpersistence modeled here and also emphasize two specific
7:229:18656:11:11:82:528:150:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:channels: the capture of the party system by the elites and the threat of violence. Both these methods were
7:230:18763:11:11:82:528:139:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:extensively used in the U.S. South after the Civil War and are still present in many Latin American countries
7:231:18872:11:10:82:528:128:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:such as Brazil, Bolivia or Colombia. For the U.S. South after the Civil War, see Key (1949), Woodward (1955),
7:232:18981:10:11:82:529:118:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:Wright (1986), Alston and Ferrie (1999), and Ransom and Sutch (2001), for Colombia, see Dix (1967), Wilde
7:233:19086:11:0:82:479:107:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:(1978), Hartlyn (1988) and Kline (1999), and for Brazil, see Chilcote (1990) and Hagopian (1996).
8:234:19184:0:18:82:529:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ments (Dixit, 1989a,b, Coate and Morris, 1999). Institutions could also persist because of the
8:235:19278:18:18:82:529:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:existence of multiple steady-state equilibria (e.g., Krugman, 1991, Matsuyama, 1991). The
8:236:19367:18:19:82:529:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:popular idea that economic inequality or certain forms of natural resource endowments tilt
8:237:19457:19:18:82:529:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the balance towards bad institutions is also different from our notion of persistence (invariance
8:238:19554:18:19:82:529:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and state dependence), since this idea stresses the persistence of economic characteristics that
8:239:19650:19:18:82:528:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:then lead to the persistence of institutions (e.g., Engerman and Sokoloff, 1997, Benabou, 2000,
8:240:19745:18:19:82:528:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:2005). None of these approaches have addressed the issues we discuss here, in particular, the
8:241:19838:19:18:82:264:571:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:coexistence of persistence and change.
8:242:19876:18:18:99:528:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:From a modeling point of view, this paper extends the framework in Acemoglu and Robin-
8:243:19962:18:19:82:528:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:son (2000, 2001, 2006a), where de facto political power drives changes in political institutions
8:244:20058:19:18:82:528:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and the future distribution of de jure political power.9The major difference is that we now
8:245:20149:18:19:82:528:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:model the process of the elite investing in their de facto political power, which leads to some
8:246:20244:19:18:82:529:479:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:significant differences in the results. While our previous work emphasized that democracy is
8:247:20336:18:18:82:533:461:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:more“pro-citizen”,theanalysishereshowsthismaynotbethecaseiftheeliteareableto
8:248:20412:18:19:82:529:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:garner sufficient de facto political power in democracy.10In this respect, the current paper is
8:249:20507:19:18:82:528:424:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:related to Mulligan, Gil and Sala-i-Martin (2004) and Mulligan and Tsui (2005), which focus
8:250:20598:18:19:82:529:406:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:on similarity of various policies between democracies and nondemocracies, though, in terms
8:251:20688:19:18:82:529:387:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of our terminology, they explain this similarity by lack of significant de jure power differences
8:252:20785:18:19:82:529:369:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:between regimes, while our model emphasizes how changes in de facto power can undo real
8:253:20872:19:18:82:207:350:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:changesindejurepower.
8:254:20893:18:18:99:529:332:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The rest of the paper is organized as follows. Section 2 outlines the basic economic and
8:255:20981:18:19:82:528:314:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political environment.  Section 3 characterizes the equilibria of the baseline model, and es-
8:256:21074:19:18:82:528:295:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tablishes the invariance result and the main comparative statics. Section 4 generalizes this
8:257:21166:18:19:82:528:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:framework in a number of directions and shows how under more general circumstances, only
8:258:21254:19:18:82:528:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:partial offset will occur, and the equilibrium will correspond to a Markov regime-switching
8:259:21345:18:19:82:529:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:model, withfluctuations between democracy and nondemocracy.  Section 5 introduces the
8:260:21430:19:18:82:529:221:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:model in which changing political institutions is more difficult than influencing economic in-
8:261:21524:18:18:82:528:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:stitutions and shows how an equilibrium pattern of captured democracy can arise with landed
8:262:21615:18:19:82:529:185:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:elites dictating their favorite economic institutions in democracy. Section 6 briefly discusses
8:263:21710:19:16:82:529:166:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:how simultaneous reforms in multiple dimensionsof political institutions or economic institu-
8:264:21803:16:11:95:528:150:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:9See also Ticchi and Vindigni (2005), Jack and Lagunoff(2006), and Lagunoff(2006) for related approaches.
8:265:21908:11:15:91:529:139:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:10See, among others, Austen-Smith (1987), Baron(1994) and Grossman and Helpman (1996) on models
8:266:22003:15:10:82:529:124:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:models where the equilibrium policy in a democracy is affected by lobbying. Our approach is more reduced-
8:267:22108:10:11:82:528:114:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:form, but explicitly models the incentives of individual agents to contribute to lobbying-type activities, is
8:268:22217:11:0:82:338:103:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:dynamic and endogenizes not just policies but also institutions.
9:269:22282:0:18:82:529:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:tions can be effective in breaking the cycle of persistence in economic institutions. Section 7
9:270:22377:18:18:82:528:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:discusses a number of historical case studies that both motivate and substantiate the ideas in
9:271:22471:18:35:82:231:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the paper. Section 8 concludes.

12:421:28104:29:26:82:391:653:145:g_d0_f4:145:g_d0_f4:C:2.2  Political Regimes and De Facto Political Power
12:422:28155:26:18:82:529:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:There are two possible political regimes, denoted byDandN, corresponding to democracy
12:423:28240:18:19:82:528:609:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and nondemocracy. The distribution of de jure political power will vary between these two
12:424:28329:19:18:82:529:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regimes. At any point in time, the “state” of this society will be represented byst∈{D,N},
12:425:28419:18:18:82:528:572:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:which designates the political regime that applies at that date. Importantly, irrespective of
12:426:28512:18:19:82:528:554:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the political regime (state), the identity of landowners and workers does not change; the same
12:427:28606:19:18:82:526:535:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:B:Mindividuals control the land, and have the potential to exercise additional political power.
12:428:28699:18:19:99:528:517:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Overall political power is determined by the interaction of de facto and de jure political
12:429:28789:19:18:82:529:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:power. Since there is a continuum of citizens, they will have difficulty in solving the collective
12:430:28887:18:18:82:528:480:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:action problem to exercise de facto political power. Consequently, we treat their de facto power
12:431:28983:18:19:82:425:462:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:as being exogenous rather than stemming from their own contributions.
12:432:29052:19:18:99:528:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In contrast, elites can spend part of their earnings to gather further de facto political power.
12:433:29148:18:19:82:529:425:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:In particular, suppose that elitei∈Espends an amountθit≥0as a contribution to activities
12:434:29236:19:18:82:528:406:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:increasing their group’s de facto power. Then total elite spending on such activities will be

12:439:29338:7:27:141:398:385:65:g_d0_f12:121:g_d0_f3:A:t, and we assume that their de facto political power is
12:440:29393:27:29:280:528:358:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:A:PEt=φZt,(13)
12:441:29405:29:18:82:529:329:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:whereφ>0.  The reason why the elite may choose to spend a positive amount on such
12:442:29486:18:19:82:528:311:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:activities is that there is afinite number,M, of them, so each of them will take into account
12:443:29579:19:18:82:529:292:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that their own contribution to total spending,Zt,willhaveaneffect on equilibrium outcomes.
12:444:29669:18:19:82:528:274:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:An important assumption implicit in (13) is that the technology for generating de facto political
12:445:29766:19:18:82:397:255:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:power for the elite is the same in democracy and nondemocracy.14
12:446:29830:18:18:99:528:237:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Even though the citizens cannot solve the collective action problem to invest in their de
12:447:29919:18:19:82:528:219:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:facto political power, since they form the majority in society they always possess some political
12:448:30016:19:18:82:528:200:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:power. The extent of this power depends on whether the political regime is democratic or
12:449:30104:18:19:82:528:182:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:nondemocratic.  We model the citizens’ total political power in a reduced-form manner as
12:450:30192:19:18:82:117:163:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:follows:
12:451:30200:18:17:249:528:145:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:A:PCt=ωt+ηI(st=D),(14)
12:452:30220:17:14:91:529:128:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:14There may be a number of reasons for why the elite’s ability to lobby and bribe politicians or use paramili-
12:453:30330:14:11:82:529:114:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:taries may be more restricted in democracy, so in Section 4, we allow this technology to differ between democracy
12:454:30443:11:0:82:160:103:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:and nondemocracy.
13:455:30462:0:18:82:528:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:whereωtis a random variable drawn independently and identically over time from a given
13:456:30548:18:18:82:529:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:distributionF(·)and measures their de facto power;I(st=D)is an indicator function for
13:457:30633:18:19:82:528:664:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:B:st=D, such thatI(st=D)=1whileI(st=N)=0;andηis a strictly positive parameter
13:458:30708:19:18:82:310:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:measuring citizens’ de jure power in democracy.
13:459:30755:18:19:99:529:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:There are two important assumptions embedded in equation (14). Thefirst is that the de
13:460:30841:19:18:82:528:608:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:facto political power of the citizensfluctuates over time, and is hard to predict in advance.15
13:461:30936:18:19:82:528:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The second assumption is that when the political regime is democratic, i.e.,st=D, citizens
13:462:31026:19:18:82:528:571:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:have greater political power. This represents in a very simple way the fact that democracy
13:463:31116:18:18:82:528:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:allocates de jure political power in favor of the majority. This will be both because of the
13:464:31208:18:19:82:528:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:formal rules of democracy and also because in democratic politics, parties may partly solve
13:465:31299:19:18:82:529:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the collective action problem of the citizens.  Put differently, equation (14) implies that in
13:466:31393:18:19:82:528:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:democracy the political power of the citizens shifts to the right in the sense offirst-order
13:467:31485:19:26:82:520:479:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:stochastic dominance. To simplify the discussion, we make the following assumptions onF:
13:468:31573:26:18:82:529:453:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:B:Assumption 2Fis defined over(ω,∞)for someω<0, is everywhere strictly increasing and
13:469:31656:18:19:110:528:435:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:twice continuously differentiable (so that its densityfand the derivative of the density,
13:470:31745:19:18:110:529:416:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:A:f0, exist everywhere). Moreover,f(ω)is single peaked (in the sense that there exists
13:471:31829:18:18:110:529:398:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:A:ω∗such thatf0(ω)>0for allω<ω∗andf0(ω)<0for allω>ω∗)andsatisfies
13:472:31892:18:26:110:197:380:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f3:A:limω→∞f(ω)=0.
13:473:31905:26:19:99:529:354:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:All of the features embedded in Assumption 2 are for convenience, and how relaxing them
13:474:31992:19:18:82:281:335:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:affects the equilibrium is discussed below.
13:475:32035:18:19:99:528:317:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:We introduce the variableπt∈{0,1}to denote whether the elite have more (total) political
13:476:32123:19:18:82:532:298:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:power. In particular, whenPEt≥PCt,wehaveπt=0andtheelitehavemorepoliticalpower
13:477:32200:18:19:82:529:280:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and will make the key decisions. In contrast, wheneverPEt<PCt,πt=1and citizens have
13:478:32283:19:18:82:365:261:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:more political power, and they will make the key decisions.
13:479:32342:18:18:99:529:243:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:To complete the description of the environment, it remains to specify what these key
13:480:32426:18:19:82:528:225:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:decisions are. We assume that the group with greater political power will decide both economic
13:481:32520:19:18:82:522:206:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:institutions at timet,τt, and what the political regime will be in the following period,st+1.
13:482:32613:18:19:99:529:188:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:When the elite have more political power, a representative elite agent makes the key deci-
13:483:32703:19:18:82:528:169:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:sions, and when citizens have more political power, a representative citizen does so. Since the
13:484:32798:18:19:82:528:151:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political preferences of all elites and all citizens are the same, these representative agents will
13:485:32897:19:14:82:320:132:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:always make the decisions favored by their group.
13:486:32946:14:15:91:528:118:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:15This assumption is used extensively in Acemoglu and Robinson (2006a), and defended there. Briefly, given
13:487:33052:15:11:82:529:103:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:their large numbers, whether and how effectively citizens will be able to organize is difficult to predict in advance,
13:488:33170:11:0:82:438:92:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:and will change from time to time. The randomness ofωtcaptures this in a simple way.
14:489:33256:0:25:82:214:700:145:g_d0_f4:145:g_d0_f4:C:2.3  Timing of Events
14:490:33277:25:18:82:409:675:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:We now briefly recap the timing of events in this basic environment.
14:491:33345:18:19:99:528:657:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:At each datet, society starts with a state variablest∈{D,N}. Given this, the following
14:492:33431:19:30:82:224:638:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:sequence of events take place:
14:493:33461:30:19:96:529:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:1. Each elite agenti∈Esimultaneously chooses how much to spend to acquire de facto
14:494:33543:19:27:110:489:589:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:political power for their group,θit≥0,andPEtis determined according to (13).
14:495:33619:27:18:96:529:562:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:2. The random variableωtis drawn from the distributionF,andPCtis determined according
14:496:33704:18:28:110:146:544:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:to (14).
14:497:33712:28:18:96:528:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:3. IfPEt≥PCt(i.e.,πt=0), a representative (e.g., randomly chosen) elite agent chooses
14:498:33797:18:28:110:503:498:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f3:A:(τt,st+1),andifPEt<PCt(i.e.,πt=1), a representative citizen chooses(τt,st+1).
14:499:33874:28:18:96:529:470:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:4. Givenτt, transactions in the labor market take place,Rtandwtare paid to elites and
14:500:33959:18:27:110:352:452:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:workers respectively, and consumption takes place.
14:501:34009:27:35:96:339:425:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:5. The following date,t+1, starts with statest+1.
14:502:34058:35:29:82:297:390:209:g_d0_f4:209:g_d0_f4:C:3  Analysis of Baseline Model
14:503:34087:29:18:82:528:361:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:We now analyze the baseline model described in the previous section. Wefirst focus on the
14:504:34176:18:19:82:529:343:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:symmetric Markov Perfect Equilibria (MPE). An MPE imposes the restriction that equilibrium
14:505:34266:19:18:82:535:324:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:strategies are mappings from payoff-relevant states, which here only includes∈{D,N}.In
14:506:34352:18:19:82:528:306:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:particular, in an MPE strategies are not conditioned on the past history of the game over and
14:507:34445:19:18:82:534:287:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:above the influence of this past history on the payoff-relevant states.AnMPEwillconsistof
14:508:34534:18:0:82:188:269:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:contribution functions
14:509:34556:0:9:192:198:278:121:g_d0_f11:121:g_d0_f11:C:©
14:510:34557:9:0:198:222:269:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f8:C:θi(s)
14:511:34562:0:14:222:228:278:121:g_d0_f11:121:g_d0_f11:C:ª
14:512:34563:14:14:229:529:264:65:g_d0_f12:121:g_d0_f3:A:i∈Efor each elite agent as a function of the political state, and
14:513:34628:14:18:82:528:250:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:decision variablesτ(π)ands0(π)as a function ofπ∈{0,1}denoting which side has more
14:514:34709:18:18:82:528:232:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f8:B:political power, and equilibrium factor prices as given by (8)-(11).16Here the functionτ(π)
14:515:34800:18:19:82:528:214:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:determines the equilibrium decision about labor repression conditional on who has power and
14:516:34891:19:18:82:529:195:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the functions0(π)∈{D,N}determines the political state at the start of the next period.
14:517:34977:18:19:82:528:177:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Symmetric MPE will in addition impose the condition that contribution functions take the
14:518:35065:19:16:82:529:158:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:formθ(s), i.e., do not depend on the identity of the individual elite,i. Symmetry is a natural
14:519:35159:16:15:91:529:142:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:16More generally, we could haveτ(π,s)ands0(π,s), so that the choice of economic institutions and future
14:520:35262:15:11:82:529:127:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:political institutions are conditioned on which party has political power,π, and the current state,s. Nevertheless,
14:521:35377:11:11:82:528:116:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:since it is clear that the current state will have no effect on these decisions, we use the more economical notation
14:522:35493:11:0:82:147:105:82:g_d0_f16:82:g_d0_f3:F:τ(π)ands0(π).
15:523:35508:0:18:82:528:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:feature here, and simplifies the analysis. We discuss asymmetric MPE for completeness below.
15:524:35600:18:18:82:352:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:A more formal definition of an MPE is also given below.
15:525:35655:18:19:99:528:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The focus on MPE is natural in this context as a way of modeling the potential collective
15:526:35744:19:18:82:529:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:action problem among the elite.  Looking at subgame perfect equilibrium (SPE) will allow
15:527:35832:18:19:82:529:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the elite greater latitude in solving the collective action problem by using implicit punishment
15:528:35928:19:29:82:338:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:strategies. We briefly analyze SPEs in subsection 3.3.
15:529:35982:29:25:82:191:579:145:g_d0_f4:145:g_d0_f4:C:3.1  Main Results
15:530:35999:25:19:82:528:554:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The MPE can be characterized by backward induction within the stage game at some arbitrary
15:531:36089:19:18:82:529:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:datet, given the states∈{D,N}. At the last stage of the game, clearly whenever the elite have
15:532:36182:18:19:82:529:517:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political power, i.e.,π=0, they will choose economic institutions that favor them, i.e.,τ=0,
15:533:36274:19:18:82:536:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and a political system that gives them more power in the future, i.e.,s0=N.Incontrast,
15:534:36360:18:18:82:528:480:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:whenever citizens have political power, i.e.,π=1, they will chooseτ=1ands0=D.17
15:535:36439:18:19:82:528:462:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:This implies that choices over economic institutions and political states are straightforward.
15:536:36533:19:18:82:528:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Moreover the determination of market prices under different economic institutions has already
15:537:36626:18:19:82:529:425:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:been specified above (recall equations (8)-(11)). Thus the only remaining decisions are the
15:538:36717:19:18:82:529:406:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:contributions of each elite agent to their de facto power,θit. Therefore, a symmetric MPE can
15:539:36810:18:19:82:529:388:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:be summarized by a level of contribution as a function of the stateθ(s). It will be convenient
15:540:36904:19:18:82:529:369:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to characterize the MPE by writing the payoffto elite agents recursively, and for this reason,
15:541:36998:18:18:82:528:351:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:we denote the equilibrium value of an elite agent in statesbyV(s)(i.e.,V(D)for democracy
15:542:37086:18:19:82:228:333:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:andV(N)for nondemocracy).
15:543:37111:19:18:99:528:314:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Let us begin with nondemocracy. Since we arefocusing on symmetric MPE, suppose that
15:544:37194:18:19:82:529:296:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:all other elite agents, excepti∈E, have chosen a level of contribution to de facto power equal
15:545:37288:19:29:82:458:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:toθ(N). Consequently, when agenti∈Echoosesθi,theirtotalpowerwillbe

15:565:37455:17:15:91:529:172:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:17We will see in Proposition 1 that the equilibrium distribution over economic institutions is the same in

19:791:44523:0:18:82:529:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:A more technical intuition for this result is that the optimal contribution conditions for elite

20:839:47543:18:18:82:528:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:isinvariancein equilibrium; even when shocks change the political institutions, the probability
20:840:47638:18:19:82:529:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:distribution over equilibrium economic institutions remains unchanged. This result also illus-
20:841:47732:19:18:82:528:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:trates how institutional change and persistence can coexist–while political institutions change
20:842:47827:18:28:82:466:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:frequently, the equilibrium process for economic institutions remains unchanged.
20:843:47907:28:18:82:529:470:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:B:Remark 1As will be discussed further below, the invariance result relies on functional form
20:844:47998:18:19:82:529:452:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:assumptions. Section 4 will show that when there are differences in the technology of generating
20:845:48094:19:18:82:528:433:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:de facto power for the elite in democracy and nondemocracy or when economic institutions are
20:846:48186:18:18:82:529:415:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:costly to change in the short run, de facto power will only offset the change in de jure power
20:847:48280:18:19:82:529:397:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:partially. Other assumptions implicit in our analysis that are important for the invariance
20:848:48371:19:18:82:529:378:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:result are: (1) that democracy shifts the power of the citizens additively (rather thanωbeing
20:849:48464:18:19:82:528:360:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:drawn from general distributionsFNin nondemocracy andFDin democracy, withFDfirst-
20:850:48545:19:18:82:529:341:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:order stochastically dominatingFN); (2) that the technology of de facto power for the elite,
20:851:48637:18:19:82:528:323:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:equation (13), is linear. When either of these assumptions are relaxed, we continue to obtain
20:852:48730:19:18:82:528:304:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the general insight that endogenous changes in de facto power (at least partially) offset declines
20:853:48828:18:28:82:505:286:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in the de jure power of the elite, but not necessarily the invariance result. See Section 4.

24:1224:56931:19:29:82:114:294:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:power.
24:1225:56937:29:25:82:274:265:145:g_d0_f4:145:g_d0_f4:C:3.3  Subgame Perfect Equilibria
24:1226:56968:25:18:82:529:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The analysis so far has focused on MPE. Since the landed elite form a small cohesive group,
24:1227:57059:18:19:82:528:222:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:they may be able to achieve a better equilibrium than the MPE by using threats of punishments
24:1228:57152:19:18:82:529:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:against each other. In this subsection, we briefly discuss SPEs (subgame perfect equilibria) of
24:1229:57247:18:19:82:528:185:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:theabovegame. Themainresultisthatforsufficiently large discount factors, the “best” SPEs
24:1230:57335:19:18:82:528:166:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:also take the same form as the MPE characterized in Propositions 1 and 2, with the equilibrium
24:1231:57429:18:19:82:496:148:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:probability distribution over economic institutions independent of the political regime.
24:1232:57517:19:18:99:529:129:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:In characterizing the SPEs, we allow elite agents to use any kind of punishment strategies
24:1233:57607:18:18:82:528:111:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and coordination, except that in competitive labor markets, they cannot (by law) restrict their
24:1234:57702:18:0:82:460:93:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f14:B:labordemandinordertoaffect factor prices. To define an SPE, letθ(st,t)≡
24:1235:57773:0:8:463:469:101:121:g_d0_f11:121:g_d0_f11:C:©
24:1236:57774:8:0:470:507:93:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f8:C:θj(st,t)
24:1237:57782:0:13:507:513:101:121:g_d0_f11:121:g_d0_f11:C:ª
24:1238:57783:13:0:514:528:88:65:g_d0_f12:65:g_d0_f18:F:j∈E
25:1239:57788:0:18:82:529:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f8:B:be the vector of contributions by elite agents at timet, when the state isst.Letht=
25:1240:57871:18:18:82:529:682:121:g_d0_f8:121:g_d0_f3:B:(θ(s0,0),π0,τ0,s1,...,θ(st,t),πt,τt,st+1)be the history of contributions, political outcomes
25:1241:57963:18:31:82:469:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and actions up to timet,withHtdenoting the set of possible histories at timet.

25:1245:58281:18:18:82:529:578:121:g_d0_f27:121:g_d0_f3:B:Z+×{0,1}×{N,D}×Ht−1→{0,1}ands0:Z+×{0,1}×{N,D}×Ht−1→{N,D}specify-
25:1246:58345:18:19:82:529:560:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ing economic and political institution decisions as a function oftime, who has political power,
25:1247:58440:19:18:82:528:541:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f18:B:the state and history, such thatθiis a best response toθ−i,τands0for alli∈Eandτands0
25:1248:58524:18:0:82:179:523:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:are best responses to
25:1249:58545:0:9:182:188:532:121:g_d0_f11:121:g_d0_f11:C:©

25:1251:58548:0:14:198:204:532:121:g_d0_f11:121:g_d0_f11:C:ª
25:1252:58549:14:26:204:529:518:65:g_d0_f12:121:g_d0_f3:A:i∈E,and factor prices are given by (8)-(11) as a function ofτ∈{0,1}.
25:1253:58617:26:18:99:529:492:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:As in most repeated and dynamic games, thereexist many subgame perfect equilibria in
25:1254:58701:18:19:82:529:474:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:this model. Our focus is on SPEs that maximize the ex ante–timet=0–utility of the elite.
25:1255:58789:19:18:82:528:455:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:This is natural since we are motivated to look at the SPEs to see how the ability of the elite
25:1256:58883:18:18:82:528:437:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to coordinate their actions changes the results. We define best or “Pareto optimal” SPEs as
25:1257:58974:18:19:82:529:419:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:SPEs in which, at timet=0, no elite agent can be made better offwithout some other elite
25:1258:59062:19:18:82:529:400:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:agent being made worse off.23In addition, we refer to an SPE as “symmetric Pareto optimal”,
25:1259:59153:18:19:82:529:382:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:if it is Pareto optimal and all elite agents use the same equilibrium strategy. The main result
25:1260:59248:19:30:82:157:363:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is the following:
25:1261:59265:30:18:82:529:333:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:B:Proposition 3(Subgame Perfect Equilibrium and Invariance)Suppose Assumptions
25:1262:59341:18:19:82:529:315:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:1-3 hold. Then there exists ̄β∈[0,1)such that that for allβ≥ ̄β, the symmetric Pareto optimal
25:1263:59434:19:18:82:529:296:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:SPE induces equilibrium probabilities of labor repressive institutionsp(D)=p(N)∈(0,1).
25:1264:59520:18:31:82:450:278:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Moreover, asβ→1, any Pareto optimal SPE involvesp(D)=p(N)∈(0,1).
25:1265:59584:31:18:99:207:247:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:A:Proof.See Appendix.
25:1266:59603:18:19:99:528:229:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:This proposition therefore shows that as long as the discount factor is large enough, the
25:1267:59692:19:18:82:528:210:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:“best” SPEs also give the same invariance result as the MPEs. Intuitively, with a high enough
25:1268:59785:18:18:82:528:192:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:discount factor, the elite act totally cohesively, as a single agent, and the same calculus as in
25:1269:59882:18:19:82:528:174:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the MPE applies for equating the marginal cost of greater contributions to de facto power to
25:1270:59974:19:18:82:529:155:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the marginal benefits, again implyingp(D)=p(N). When the discount factor is sufficiently
25:1271:60062:18:19:82:528:137:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:small, however, this result may no longer be true, because a different pattern of contributions
25:1272:60157:19:16:82:529:118:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:may be necessary to ensure “incentive compatibility” on the side of the elite agents (i.e., to
25:1273:60251:16:0:91:515:102:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:23Clearly, here Pareto optimality is only among the elite and does not consider the utility of the citizens.
26:1274:60361:0:18:82:528:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ensure that certain elite agents are willing to make the contributions they are supposed to
26:1275:60452:18:29:82:245:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:make along the equilibrium path).
26:1276:60485:29:25:82:232:653:145:g_d0_f4:145:g_d0_f4:C:3.4  Comparative Statics

28:1417:65019:19:18:99:528:402:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Many of the comparative statics in Proposition 4 are intuitive, and yet quite useful in terms
28:1418:65112:18:19:82:528:384:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:of economic implications. For example, the fact that an increase in∆Rinduces both greater
28:1419:65201:19:18:82:528:365:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:contributions by elite agents and also increases the probability that they control political
28:1420:65293:18:18:82:528:347:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:power is very intuitive, since∆Ris a measure of how much they have to gain by controlling
28:1421:65382:18:19:82:528:329:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political power. The greater is this gain, the more willing is each elite agent to contribute to
28:1422:65478:19:18:82:529:310:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:their collective political power.24Since∆Rwill be high whenAis low, Proposition 4 also
28:1423:65564:18:19:82:529:292:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:implies∂p∗/∂A <0. In other words, in a society where alternative (e.g., proto-industrial)
28:1424:65653:19:18:82:529:273:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:economic activities are less developed and where, by repressing labor the elite can obtain
28:1425:65743:18:19:82:529:255:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:large rents, political and economic institutions are more likely to be controlled by the elite,
28:1426:65838:19:18:82:529:236:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and consequently economic institutions are more likely to be tilted towards repressive labor
28:1427:65930:18:18:82:322:218:121:g_d0_f3:65:g_d0_f3:B:relations rather than competitive labor markets.25
28:1428:65980:18:19:99:528:200:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Thefactthatahigherβalso increases contributions by the elite and the likelihood of labor
28:1429:66068:19:18:82:529:181:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:repressive institutions is also interesting. Inmany models, a higher discount factor leads to
28:1430:66161:18:19:82:528:163:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:better allocations. Here, in contrast, a higher discount factor leads to more wasteful activities
28:1431:66258:19:15:82:528:144:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:by the elite and labor repressive economic institutions. The reason is that the main pivotal
28:1432:66350:15:15:91:529:129:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:24Thisfinding is also in line with the empirical literature on collective action whichfinds that it is more likely
28:1433:66464:15:7:82:276:114:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:when the benefits are higher (e.g., Wade, 1988).
28:1434:66512:7:15:91:529:107:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:25The fact that the elite can never impose slavery, thus taking away the outside option of the workers, is
28:1435:66618:15:0:82:292:92:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:naturally important for the result that∂p∗/∂A <0.
29:1436:66669:0:18:82:528:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:agents in this model are the elite, which, by virtue of their smaller numbers, take the effect of
29:1437:66766:18:18:82:529:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:their contributions on equilibrium allocationsinto account. Contributing to de facto political
29:1438:66860:18:19:82:528:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:power is a form of investment, and some of the returns accrue to the elite in the future (when
29:1439:66954:19:18:82:529:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:they secure nondemocracy instead of democracy). Therefore a higher level ofβencourages
29:1440:67040:18:19:82:528:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:them to invest more in their political power and makes nondemocracy and labor repressive
29:1441:67128:19:18:82:242:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:economic institutions more likely.
29:1442:67162:18:19:99:529:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The third set of comparative statics show that whenMincreases so that there are more
29:1443:67246:19:18:82:528:571:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:elite agents, the collective action problem among them becomes worse. This highlights the
29:1444:67335:18:18:82:529:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:latent free-rider problem in the model. Even though each elite agent contributes to the group’s
29:1445:67430:18:19:82:528:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political power, their level of contribution is still suboptimal from the viewpoint of the group,
29:1446:67527:19:18:82:529:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:since each elite agent realizes that by contributing more he creates a positive externality on
29:1447:67621:18:19:82:528:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:other elites. A greaterMincreases the extent of this positive externality and intensifies the
29:1448:67714:19:18:82:528:479:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:free-rider problem (the collective action problem). This comparative static therefore suggests
29:1449:67808:18:18:82:528:461:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that nondemocracy and labor repressive economic institutions are more likely to emerge when
29:1450:67899:18:19:82:528:443:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:there is a relatively small and cohesive group of elite land owners, a pattern consistent with
29:1451:67993:19:18:82:285:424:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:the historical case studies discussed below.
29:1452:68037:18:19:99:529:406:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The most surprising comparative static results are those with respect toη. Recall that a
29:1453:68125:19:18:82:529:387:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:higherηcorresponds to democracy giving more de jure power to the citizens. We may have
29:1454:68211:18:19:82:529:369:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:therefore expected a greaterηto lead to better outcomes for the citizens. In contrast, wefind
29:1455:68304:19:18:82:529:350:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that higherηmakes nondemocracy and labor repressive economic institutions more likely (as
29:1456:68393:18:18:82:529:332:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:long as Assumption 3 still holds). The reason for this is that a higherηmakes democracy
29:1457:68480:18:19:82:528:314:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:more costly for the elite, so it is in the interest of each elite agent to invest more in the group’s
29:1458:68581:19:18:82:528:295:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:political power to avoid democracy. This effect is strong enough to increase the probability
29:1459:68673:18:19:82:529:277:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that they will maintain political power. However, the overall impact ofηon the likelihood of
29:1460:68765:19:18:82:528:258:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:democracy is non-monotonic: ifηincreases so much that Assumption 3 no longer holds, then
29:1461:68853:18:19:82:522:240:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Corollary 1 applies and democracy may become fully consolidated (i.e., an absorbing state).
29:1462:68944:19:18:99:529:221:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Note however that both the results that higherMreduces the political power of the elite
29:1463:69031:18:18:82:529:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:and that higherηincreases their political power depend on the functional form assumptions
29:1464:69120:18:19:82:529:185:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:already highlighted in Remark 1.26Nevertheless, we believe that the baseline model we have
29:1465:69210:19:16:82:514:166:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is both the simplest and the most natural one, and highlights importantfirst-order effects.
29:1466:69301:16:15:91:531:150:36:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:26In particular, both the additive shift of the distribution function ofωindemocracyandthefactthat(13)is
29:1467:69405:15:11:82:528:135:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:linear are important for these comparative statics. The fact that the effect ofMonp∗is ambiguous in general
29:1468:69512:11:10:82:532:124:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:is related to Esteban and Ray (2001), who emphasize that the effectofanincreaseinthenumberofagents
29:1469:69610:10:11:82:528:114:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:to the total contribution of a lobby is ambiguous because, while each agent contributes less, there are more of
29:1470:69721:11:0:82:105:103:82:g_d0_f3:82:g_d0_f3:F:them.
30:1471:69728:0:18:99:528:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, whenφincreases, the technology of garnering de facto political power for the
30:1472:69813:18:18:82:528:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:elite improves. This may reduce their contributions to the group’s de facto power, but it will
30:1473:69907:18:19:82:529:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:always increase the equilibrium probability of a nondemocratic regimeand labor repressive
30:1474:69996:19:34:82:139:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:institutions.
30:1475:70009:34:18:82:535:611:209:g_d0_f4:209:g_d0_f4:C:4  Generalizations: Markov Regime-Switching Models and State
30:1476:70069:18:29:106:191:593:209:g_d0_f4:209:g_d0_f4:C:Dependence
30:1477:70079:29:19:82:528:564:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The model in the previous section yielded stark results, which were partly driven by the
30:1478:70167:19:18:82:528:545:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:assumptions that the elite had the same technology to generate de facto political power in both
30:1479:70262:18:18:82:528:527:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regimes and were able to change economic institutions immediately after they took control (in
30:1480:70355:18:19:82:528:509:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:addition to the functional form assumption noted in footnote 26). Relaxing these assumptions
30:1481:70447:19:18:82:528:490:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:leads to a richer form of persistence, in the form of a Markov regime-switching model with
30:1482:70537:18:19:82:528:472:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:state dependence. These issues are discussed in the next two subsections, and also pave the
30:1483:70628:19:18:82:487:453:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:way of our analysis of how to effectively reform equilibrium institutions in Section 6.
30:1484:70715:18:18:99:528:435:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Another special feature of the model in the previous section was that it implicitly assumed
30:1485:70806:18:19:82:528:417:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that changing economic institutions and changing the political system were equally easy (or
30:1486:70897:19:18:82:529:398:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:difficult). An extension in which changing political institutions may require greater political
30:1487:70992:18:19:82:470:380:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:power than influencing economic policies or institutions is discussed in Section 5.
30:1488:71075:19:29:99:528:361:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Throughout the rest of the paper, to simplify the discussion, we focus on symmetric MPE.
30:1489:71163:29:25:82:337:332:145:g_d0_f4:145:g_d0_f4:C:4.1  Limits on De Facto Power of the Elite
30:1490:71205:25:19:82:529:307:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Ourfirst generalization of the above framework assumes that in democracy, because of limits
30:1491:71296:19:27:82:528:288:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:on the activities of the elite, their technology for gathering de facto political power changes to
30:1492:71394:27:28:266:528:261:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:A:PEt(D)=φDZt,(34)
30:1493:71410:28:0:82:213:233:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f8:B:whereφD∈(0,φ)andZt=
30:1494:71429:0:11:216:228:241:121:g_d0_f11:121:g_d0_f11:C:P
30:1495:71430:11:0:227:248:230:65:g_d0_f12:121:g_d0_f9:C:i∈Eθ
30:1496:71434:0:8:248:251:238:65:g_d0_f12:65:g_d0_f12:F:i
30:1497:71435:8:0:248:255:230:65:g_d0_f12:121:g_d0_f3:A:t.
30:1498:71437:0:22:255:528:237:65:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:27In other words, each unit of thefinal good spent by the
30:1499:71494:22:19:82:528:215:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:elite for increasing their de facto power is less effective in democracy than in nondemocracy.
30:1500:71588:19:18:82:528:196:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:This is a reasonable assumption, since democraticinstitutions may prevent the elite from using
30:1501:71682:18:19:82:529:178:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:repression or paramilitaries or from buying politicians as effectively as in a nondemocratic
30:1502:71774:19:18:82:528:159:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regime.  Therefore, in this model democracy has two simultaneous functions; it shifts the
30:1503:71863:18:18:82:528:141:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of de jure political powers towards the citizens and it limits the exercise of de
30:1504:71957:18:16:82:198:123:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:facto power by the elite.

35:1813:81877:26:18:82:528:184:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Next we modify the above framework in a different direction, and assume that starting in
35:1814:81965:18:18:82:528:166:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:democracy, the elite cannot impose their favorite economic institutions immediately, for exam-
35:1815:82059:18:19:82:529:148:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ple, democratic politics has already taken some actions that cannot be reversed within the same
35:1816:82154:19:18:82:529:129:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:period. This implies that starting in democracy,economic institutions are “slow-changing” or

35:1818:82342:19:0:82:474:92:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:cost when they change economic institutions from competitive to labor repressive.

39:2053:87535:0:18:99:528:700:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:This proposition shows that in the environment with sluggish economic institutions the
39:2054:87621:18:18:82:529:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:main comparative static results from Proposition 4 regarding the effect of economic rents, the
39:2055:87715:18:19:82:528:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:discount factor and the cohesion of the landed elite continue to apply. Also interestingly, a
39:2056:87808:19:18:82:529:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:decrease inλ, meaning more sluggish economic institutions in democracy, increasesp∗(N).
39:2057:87895:18:19:82:529:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:This is intuitive; a lowerλmeans that democracy is more costly for the elite, because it will
39:2058:87988:19:18:82:528:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:take time for them to impose their favorite economic institutions even when they take control
39:2059:88081:18:19:82:529:590:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in democracy. Consequently, the value of nondemocracy relative to democracy,V(N)−V(D),
39:2060:88167:19:18:82:529:571:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is higher, so in nondemocracy, the elite investmore in order to preserve this set of political
39:2061:88261:18:18:82:528:553:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:institutions (and the associated labor repressive economic institutions). The implications of
39:2062:88354:18:19:82:529:535:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:a decrease inλon the elite’s de facto power in democracy is ambiguous, since it reduces the
39:2063:88445:19:18:82:532:516:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:immediate benefits of taking control in democracy, but also, by increasingV(N)−V(D),it
39:2064:88531:18:35:82:231:498:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:increases the long-run benefits.
39:2065:88563:35:29:82:500:463:209:g_d0_f4:209:g_d0_f4:C:5  Durable Political Institutions and Captured Democracy
39:2066:88619:29:18:82:528:434:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:The assumption so far has been that when the elite have more political power than the citizens,
39:2067:88714:18:19:82:528:416:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:they can change both economic institutions and the political system (though in the previous
39:2068:88805:19:18:82:528:397:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:subsection, they could only change the economic institutions slowly). The historical examples
39:2069:88898:18:18:82:528:379:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f7:B:below illustrate a different salient pattern: democracy may emerge and endure, but in acap-
39:2070:88989:18:19:82:528:361:121:g_d0_f7:121:g_d0_f3:B:turedform, whereby the elite are able to impose their favorite economic institutions (or at the
39:2071:89084:19:18:82:528:342:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:very least, have a disproportionate effect on the choice of economic institutions) in an enduring
39:2072:89181:18:19:82:529:324:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:democracy. It is therefore important to generalize the model so that there can be differences
39:2073:89274:19:18:82:350:305:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:between equilibrium political and economic institutions.
39:2074:89330:18:19:99:529:287:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:As discussed in detail in Acemoglu and Robinson (2006a), in many situations, political
39:2075:89416:19:18:82:529:268:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:institutions are more difficult to change, and may have additional “durability”. We now mod-
39:2076:89508:18:18:82:529:250:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ify the baseline model to incorporate this feature and assume that overthrowing a democratic
39:2077:89600:18:19:82:529:232:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:regime is more difficult than influencing economic institutions.  More specifically, the elite
39:2078:89694:19:18:82:529:213:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:require greater political power to force a switch from democracy to nondemocracy than sim-
39:2079:89784:18:19:82:528:195:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:ply influencing economic institutions in democracy.  To simplify the discussion, we assume
39:2080:89874:19:18:82:528:176:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:that when they influence economic institutions in democracy, they can choose their favorite
39:2081:89965:18:19:82:269:158:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:economic institutions, labor repression.

42:2288:95286:30:18:99:533:305:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:Given this definition, a symmetric MPE withθ(N)>0andθ(D)>0isasolutiontothe
42:2289:95360:18:29:82:194:287:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:following two equations

42:2299:95519:18:19:509:528:203:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:(57)
42:2300:95523:19:18:82:529:184:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:It can be verified that Assumption 3 above is sufficient to ensure that zero contributions cannot
42:2301:95620:18:18:82:144:166:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:be equilibria.
42:2302:95634:18:19:99:528:148:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:A:The interesting result in this case is that once the society becomes democratic, it will
42:2303:95722:19:18:82:532:129:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:remain so potentially for a long time (i.e.,ˆp(D)canbesmall),buttheelitewillstillbeableto
42:2304:95811:18:19:82:529:111:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:control the economic institutions (i.e.,p(D)could be quite large). This is stated and proved
42:2305:95903:19:0:82:195:92:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in the next proposition.
43:2306:95929:0:18:82:528:700:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:B:Proposition 9(Captured Democracy)Consider the modified model with durable political
43:2307:96012:18:18:82:528:682:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:institutions. Suppose that Assumptions 1, 2’ and 3 hold. Then we have a Markov regime-
43:2308:96098:18:19:82:529:664:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:switching process with state dependence and1>ˆp(N)>ˆp(D)>0. Moreover, democracy
43:2309:96177:19:18:82:529:645:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:is captured in the sense that0<p(N)<p(D)<1, i.e., democracy will survive but choose
43:2310:96260:18:19:82:528:627:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:economic institutions in line with the elite’s interests with even a higher probability than does
43:2311:96357:19:30:82:153:608:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:nondemocracy.
43:2312:96370:30:29:99:505:578:121:g_d0_f4:121:g_d0_f3:A:Proof.The probability of labor repressive economic institutions under democracy is
43:2313:96452:29:29:190:421:549:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f9:C:p(D)=p(θ(D),θ(D)|D)=F(φMθ(D)−η),
43:2314:96484:29:19:82:129:520:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:while it is
43:2315:96495:19:24:200:410:501:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f8:C:p(N)=p(θ(N),θ(N)|N)=F(φMθ(N))
43:2316:96524:24:19:82:532:477:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:in nondemocracy. Suppose, to obtain a contradiction, thatp(D)≤p(N). Thisisequivalent
43:2317:96608:19:18:82:92:458:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:to
43:2318:96610:18:25:243:528:440:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f3:A:φMθ(D)−η≤φMθ(N).(58)
43:2319:96630:25:29:82:397:415:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Since from Assumption 2’fis decreasing everywhere, this implies
43:2320:96693:29:30:226:385:386:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f9:C:f(φMθ(D)−η)≥f(φMθ(N)).
43:2321:96715:30:29:82:349:356:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:This equation combined with (56) and (57) implies that
43:2322:96769:29:29:207:404:327:121:g_d0_f9:121:g_d0_f9:C:f(φMθ(D)−η−ξ)≤f(φMθ(N)+ξ).
43:2323:96795:29:29:82:380:298:121:g_d0_f3:121:g_d0_f3:B:Since from Assumption 2’fis decreasing, this is equivalent to
